//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/High_and_Low_Altitude_ENAME_Terminal_Europe_Vol_3-10100.jpg/440px-High_and_Low_Altitude_ENAME_Terminal_Europe_Vol_3-10100.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3519" data-file-height="5165" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:High_and_Low_Altitude_ENAME_Terminal_Europe_Vol_3-10100.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>FAA airport diagram</div></div></div>\n<p><b>Frankfurt Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>FRA</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EDDF</b>) (German: <i lang="de">Flughafen Frankfurt am Main</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[\xcb\x88flu\xcb\x90kha\xcb\x90fn\xcc\xa9 \xcb\x8cf\xca\x81a\xc5\x8bkf\xca\x8a\xca\x81t \xca\x94am \xcb\x88ma\xc9\xaan]</a></span>, also known as <i>Rhein-Main-Flughafen</i>) is a major <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, the fifth-largest city of <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and one of the world\'s leading financial centres. It is operated by <a href="/wiki/Fraport" title="Fraport">Fraport</a> and serves as the <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">main hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> including <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_CityLine" title="Lufthansa CityLine">Lufthansa CityLine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Cargo" title="Lufthansa Cargo">Lufthansa Cargo</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Condor_Flugdienst" class="mw-redirect" title="Condor Flugdienst">Condor</a> and <a href="/wiki/AeroLogic" title="AeroLogic">AeroLogic</a>. The airport covers an area of 2,300 hectares (5,683 acres) of land<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and features two passenger terminals with a capacity of approximately 65&#160;million passengers per year, four runways and extensive logistics and maintenance facilities.\n</p><p>Frankfurt Airport is the busiest airport by passenger traffic in Germany, as well as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">4th busiest in Europe</a> after <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London\xe2\x80\x93Heathrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris\xe2\x80\x93Charles de Gaulle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a>. The airport is also the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by passenger traffic">13th busiest worldwide</a> by total number of passengers in 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> with 60.786&#160;million passengers using the airport in 2016. In 2017, Frankfurt Airport handled 64.5&#160;million passengers and nearly 70&#160;million in 2018. It also had a freight throughput of 2.076&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">metric tonnes</a> in 2015 and is the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_cargo_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by cargo traffic">busiest airport in Europe by cargo traffic</a>. As of summer 2017, Frankfurt Airport serves more than 300 destinations in 5 continents, making it the airport with the most direct routes in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The southern side of the airport ground was home to the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Main_Air_Base" title="Rhein-Main Air Base">Rhein-Main Air Base</a>, which was a major <a href="/wiki/Air_base" title="Air base">air base</a> for the United States from 1947 until 2005, when the air base was closed and the property was acquired by Fraport (now occupied by Terminal 3). In 2017, passengers at the airport increased by 6.1% to 64,500,386 compared to 2016. The airport celebrated its 80th anniversary in July 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-52"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-53"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-54"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Frankfurt Airport lies 12&#160;km (7.5&#160;mi) southwest of <a href="/wiki/Innenstadt_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Innenstadt (Frankfurt am Main)">central Frankfurt</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AIP_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AIP-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> near the <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">Autobahn</a> intersection <a href="/wiki/Frankfurter_Kreuz" title="Frankfurter Kreuz">Frankfurter Kreuz</a>, where two of the most heavily used motorways in Europe (<a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_3" title="Bundesautobahn 3">A3</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_5" title="Bundesautobahn 5">A5</a>) meet. The airport grounds, which form a city district of Frankfurt named <a href="/wiki/Flughafen_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" class="mw-redirect" title="Flughafen (Frankfurt am Main)">Frankfurt-Flughafen</a>, are surrounded by the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_City_Forest" title="Frankfurt City Forest">Frankfurt City Forest</a>. The southern portion of the airport grounds extend partially into the cities of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCsselsheim_am_Main" title="R\xc3\xbcsselsheim am Main">R\xc3\xbcsselsheim am Main</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6rfelden-Walldorf" title="M\xc3\xb6rfelden-Walldorf">M\xc3\xb6rfelden-Walldorf</a>, and a western portion of the grounds lie within the city of <a href="/wiki/Kelsterbach" title="Kelsterbach">Kelsterbach</a>.\n</p><p>The airport is centrally located in the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt/Rhine-Main" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankfurt/Rhine-Main">Frankfurt/Rhine-Main region</a>, Germany\'s <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_regions_in_Germany" title="Metropolitan regions in Germany">third-largest metropolitan region</a>, which itself has a central location in the densely populated region of the <a href="/wiki/Blue_Banana" title="Blue Banana">west-central European megalopolis</a>. Thereby, along with a strong <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_long-distance_station" title="Frankfurt Airport long-distance station">rail</a> and motorway connection, the airport serves as a major transport node for the greater region, less than two hours by ground to <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruhr Area">Ruhr Area</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The base opened as a German commercial airport in 1936, with the northern part of the base used as a field for fixed-wing aircraft and the extreme southern part near <a href="/wiki/Zeppelinheim" class="mw-redirect" title="Zeppelinheim">Zeppelinheim</a> serving as a base for rigid airships. That section of Rhein-Main later became the base for the <a href="/wiki/LZ_127_Graf_Zeppelin" title="LZ 127 Graf Zeppelin">Graf Zeppelin</a>, its sister ship <a href="/wiki/LZ_130_Graf_Zeppelin" class="mw-redirect" title="LZ 130 Graf Zeppelin">LZ-130</a>, and, until 6 May 1937, for the ill-fated <a href="/wiki/LZ_129_Hindenburg" title="LZ 129 Hindenburg">Hindenburg</a>.\n</p><p>The airships were dismantled and their huge hangars demolished on 6 May 1940 during conversion of the base to military use. <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> engineers subsequently extended the single runway, and erected hangars and other facilities for German military aircraft. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the Luftwaffe used the field sporadically as a fighter base and as an experimental station for jet aircraft.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_airport">First airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 16 November 1909, the <a href="/wiki/DELAG" title="DELAG">world\'s first airline</a> was founded in Frankfurt am Main: The <i>Deutsche Luftschiffahrts-Aktiengesellschaft</i> (<a href="/wiki/DELAG" title="DELAG">DELAG</a>). DELAG then built the first airport in Frankfurt, called <i>Airship Base at Rebstock</i>, which was located in <a href="/wiki/Bockenheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Bockenheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Bockenheim</a> in the western part of the city and was primarily used for <a href="/wiki/Airship" title="Airship">airships</a> in the beginning. It opened in 1912 and was extended after <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, but in 1924 an expert\'s report already questioned the possibility of further expansions at this location.\n</p><p>With the foundation of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Luft_Hansa" title="Deutsche Luft Hansa">Deutsche Luft Hansa</a> in 1926 a rapid boom of civilian air travel started and soon the airship base became too small to handle the demand. Plans for a new and larger airport located in the Frankfurt City Forest south-west of <a href="/wiki/Schwanheim_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Schwanheim (Frankfurt am Main)">Schwanheim</a> were approved in 1930, but were not realised due to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>. After the <i><a href="/wiki/Machtergreifung" class="mw-redirect" title="Machtergreifung">Machtergreifung</a></i> in 1933 the government revived the plans and started the construction of the new airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_airport">Second airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Second airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r,_a_h%C3%A1tt%C3%A9rben_egy_Zeppelin_hang%C3%A1r._Fortepan_73099.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_a_h%C3%A1tt%C3%A9rben_egy_Zeppelin_hang%C3%A1r._Fortepan_73099.jpg/220px-Rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_a_h%C3%A1tt%C3%A9rben_egy_Zeppelin_hang%C3%A1r._Fortepan_73099.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_a_h%C3%A1tt%C3%A9rben_egy_Zeppelin_hang%C3%A1r._Fortepan_73099.jpg/330px-Rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_a_h%C3%A1tt%C3%A9rben_egy_Zeppelin_hang%C3%A1r._Fortepan_73099.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_a_h%C3%A1tt%C3%A9rben_egy_Zeppelin_hang%C3%A1r._Fortepan_73099.jpg/440px-Rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r%2C_a_h%C3%A1tt%C3%A9rben_egy_Zeppelin_hang%C3%A1r._Fortepan_73099.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6702" data-file-height="4240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rep%C3%BCl%C5%91t%C3%A9r,_a_h%C3%A1tt%C3%A9rben_egy_Zeppelin_hang%C3%A1r._Fortepan_73099.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Frankfurt Airport in 1936, with one Ju 86, two Ju 52/3ms and one Fw 200 of Deutsche Lufthansa</div></div></div>\n<p>A two-storey station building with a six-storey tower originated in 1935 on the northern part of the airport, as well as other operating and outbuildings for maintenance and storage of aircraft. The approximately 100 hectares <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runway</a> received a grass cover.\n</p><p>The official opening of the new <i> Flug- und Luftschiffhafen Rhein-Main</i> took place on 8 July 1936. The first plane that landed was a <a href="/wiki/Junkers_Ju_52" title="Junkers Ju 52">Ju 52/3m</a>. Six days later, on 14 July 1936, <a href="/wiki/LZ_127" class="mw-redirect" title="LZ 127">LZ 127</a> <i>Graf Zeppelin </i>landed at the airport. In 1936, 800 tons of cargo and 58,000 passengers were transported, and in 1937 these figures increased to 70,000 passengers and 966 tons of cargo. In the coming years, the new airport was the home base for the two largest German airships LZ 127 <i>Graf Zeppelin </i>and <a href="/wiki/LZ_129" class="mw-redirect" title="LZ 129">LZ 129</a> <i>Hindenburg</i>. In 1938, Frankfurt was a central distribution point for the transport of airmail to North America.\n</p><p>On 6 May 1937, the <i>Hindenburg, </i>flying from Frankfurt to <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindenburg_disaster" title="Hindenburg disaster">exploded</a> shortly before it was scheduled to dock at <a href="/wiki/Naval_Air_Engineering_Station_Lakehurst" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval Air Engineering Station Lakehurst">Lakehurst</a>. 36 people died. The accident marked the end of scheduled airship traffic and the end of the <a href="/wiki/Airship" title="Airship">airship</a> era.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After the beginning of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in 1939, all foreign airlines left the airport and control of air traffic was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a>. On 9 May 1940, the first <a href="/wiki/Bomber" title="Bomber">bombers</a> took off to attack France. From August to November 1944, a <a href="/wiki/Concentration_camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentration camp">concentration camp</a> was established in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6rfelden-Walldorf" title="M\xc3\xb6rfelden-Walldorf">Walldorf</a>, close to the airport site, where Jewish female prisoners were forced to work for the airport. The <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies of World War II</a> destroyed the runway system with <a href="/wiki/Airstrike" title="Airstrike">airstrikes</a> in 1944 and the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> blew up buildings and fuel depots in 1945, shortly before the <a href="/wiki/US_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="US Army">US Army</a> took control of the airport on 25 March 1945. After the <a href="/wiki/German_Instrument_of_Surrender" title="German Instrument of Surrender">German Instrument of Surrender</a>, the war in Europe ended and the US Army started to build a new temporary runway at Frankfurt Airport. The southern part of the airport ground was occupied to build the <a href="/wiki/Rhein-Main_Air_Base" title="Rhein-Main Air Base">Rhein-Main Air Base</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Force Base">Air Force Base</a> for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Forces_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Air Forces in Europe">United States Air Forces in Europe</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Berlin_Airlift">Berlin Airlift</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Berlin Airlift">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlinairlift-rm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Berlinairlift-rm.jpg/220px-Berlinairlift-rm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Berlinairlift-rm.jpg/330px-Berlinairlift-rm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Berlinairlift-rm.jpg/440px-Berlinairlift-rm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="313" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlinairlift-rm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rhein-Main Air Base during the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Airlift" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Airlift">Berlin Airlift</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1948, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> blocked the Western Allies\' rail and road access to the sectors of <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> under Allied control. Their aim was to force the western powers to allow the Soviet zone to start supplying Berlin with food and fuel, thereby giving the Soviets practical control over the entire city. In response, the Western Allies organised the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Airlift" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Airlift">Berlin Airlift</a> to carry supplies via air to the people in West Berlin. The airports in Frankfurt, <a href="/wiki/Hamburg_Airport" title="Hamburg Airport">Hamburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hannover_Airport" title="Hannover Airport">Hannover</a> were the primary bases for Allied aircraft. The heavy use of these so-called "<a href="/wiki/Raisin_Bombers" title="Raisin Bombers">Raisin Bombers</a>" caused damage to the runway in Frankfurt and forced the US Army to build a second parallel runway. The airlift ended in September 1949 after the Soviet Union ended their blockade.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth_of_the_airport">Growth of the airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Growth of the airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhein-Main_1951.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rhein-Main_1951.jpg/220px-Rhein-Main_1951.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="327" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rhein-Main_1951.jpg/330px-Rhein-Main_1951.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rhein-Main_1951.jpg/440px-Rhein-Main_1951.jpg 2x" data-file-width="995" data-file-height="1478" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rhein-Main_1951.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Civil air traffic at Frankfurt Airport in 1951</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iran_Air_Boeing_707-300_Manteufel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Iran_Air_Boeing_707-300_Manteufel.jpg/220px-Iran_Air_Boeing_707-300_Manteufel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Iran_Air_Boeing_707-300_Manteufel.jpg/330px-Iran_Air_Boeing_707-300_Manteufel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Iran_Air_Boeing_707-300_Manteufel.jpg/440px-Iran_Air_Boeing_707-300_Manteufel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="682" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iran_Air_Boeing_707-300_Manteufel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Iran_Air" title="Iran Air">Iran Air</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707</a>\xe2\x80\x93320B at Frankfurt Airport in 1970</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1951, restrictions for German air travellers were lifted and civil air traffic started to grow again. In 1952, Frankfurt Airport handled more than 400,000 passengers; a year later it was more than half a million. About 100 to 120 aeroplanes took off from and landed in Frankfurt daily. In 1955, Lufthansa resumed flights to and from Frankfurt and in the same year the Federal Republic of Germany gained its <a href="/wiki/Air_sovereignty" title="Air sovereignty">air sovereignty</a> back from the Allies. In 1957, the northern runway was extended, first to 3,000&#160;m (9,843&#160;ft) and then to 3,900&#160;m (12,795&#160;ft), to make it compatible with <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">jet aircraft</a>.\n</p><p>The airport did not emerge as a major international <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">airline hub</a> until 1958 when a new passenger terminal called <i>Empfangsanlage Ost</i> (Terminal East, literally "Arrival Facility East") opened in the north-east corner of the airport site. Only four years later it was clear that the terminal was already too small for the demand. In 1961, Frankfurt already had 2.2&#160;million passengers and 81,000 take-offs and landings, making it the second busiest airport in Europe behind <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a>, London.\n</p><p>In 1962, it was decided to build an even larger terminal with a capacity of 30&#160;million passengers per year. Work on this terminal began in 1965. The southern runway was extended to 3,750&#160;m (12,303&#160;ft) in 1964. In 1970, a new hangar was inaugurated; this accommodated six jet aircraft and was the world\'s largest hangar at the time.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_new_main_terminal">The new main terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The new main terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flughafen_Frankfurt_am_Main_-_Gate_A_-_Check-In_0212.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Flughafen_Frankfurt_am_Main_-_Gate_A_-_Check-In_0212.jpg/220px-Flughafen_Frankfurt_am_Main_-_Gate_A_-_Check-In_0212.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Flughafen_Frankfurt_am_Main_-_Gate_A_-_Check-In_0212.jpg/330px-Flughafen_Frankfurt_am_Main_-_Gate_A_-_Check-In_0212.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Flughafen_Frankfurt_am_Main_-_Gate_A_-_Check-In_0212.jpg/440px-Flughafen_Frankfurt_am_Main_-_Gate_A_-_Check-In_0212.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1290" data-file-height="1009" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flughafen_Frankfurt_am_Main_-_Gate_A_-_Check-In_0212.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Check-in concourse A in Terminal 1</div></div></div>\n<p>The new terminal, called <i>Terminal Mitte</i> (Central Terminal, today known as Terminal 1) is divided into three concourses (A, B and C) with 56 gates and an electric <a href="/wiki/Baggage_handling_system" title="Baggage handling system">baggage handling system</a>. Everything opened to the public on 14 March 1972. It was assumed that the terminal capacity would be sufficient for the next 30 years. Along with the new terminal a railway station (Frankfurt Airport station) was opened, the first airport railway station in the Federal Republic of Germany. A few days later the old <i>Empfangsanlage Ost</i> was closed.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_third_runway">The third runway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The third runway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Planning for a third runway (called <i><a href="/wiki/Runway_18_West" title="Runway 18 West">Startbahn 18 West</a></i>) began in 1973. This project spawned massive protests by residents and environmentalists. The main points of conflict were increasing noise and pollution and the cutting down of protected trees in the Frankfurt City Forest. While the protests and related lawsuits were unsuccessful in preventing construction, the <i>Startbahn West</i> protests were one of the major crystallisation points for the German <a href="/wiki/Environmental_movement" title="Environmental movement">environmental movement</a> of the 1980s. The protests even continued after the runway had been opened in 1984 and in 1987 two police officers were killed by a gunman. This incident ended the <i>Startbahn West</i> protests for good. Because of its orientation in the north\xe2\x80\x93south direction, in contrast to the other east\xe2\x80\x93west runways, the use of the third runway is limited. The Startbahn West can only be used for takeoffs to the south to avoid interference with air traffic on the other runways. Owing to this restriction the runway must be partially or fully closed when northward winds are too strong.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2_and_the_second_railway_station">Terminal 2 and the second railway station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Terminal 2 and the second railway station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airport_FRA_2010-06-06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Airport_FRA_2010-06-06.jpg/220px-Airport_FRA_2010-06-06.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Airport_FRA_2010-06-06.jpg/330px-Airport_FRA_2010-06-06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Airport_FRA_2010-06-06.jpg/440px-Airport_FRA_2010-06-06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airport_FRA_2010-06-06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The apron of Terminal 2</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1990, work on a new terminal (<i>Terminal 2</i>) began because it was anticipated that <i>Terminal Mitte</i> would reach its capacity limit sooner than expected. The new terminal, divided into concourses D and E, was built to the east of the existing terminal where once the <i>Empfangsanlage Ost</i> had been. With its opening in 1994, Frankfurt Airport increased its terminal capacity to 54&#160;million passengers per year. Along with the terminal opening, a <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">people mover</a> system called <i>Sky Line</i> was established to provide a fast connection between <i>Terminal 2</i> and <i>Terminal Mitte</i> (now renamed <i>Terminal 1</i>).\n</p><p>In 1999 a second railway station, primarily for <a href="/wiki/InterCityExpress" class="mw-redirect" title="InterCityExpress">InterCityExpress</a> long-distance trains (called <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_long-distance_station" title="Frankfurt Airport long-distance station">Frankfurt Airport long-distance station</a>), opened near Terminal 1 as part of the new <a href="/wiki/Cologne%E2%80%93Frankfurt_high-speed_rail_line" title="Cologne\xe2\x80\x93Frankfurt high-speed rail line">Cologne\xe2\x80\x93Frankfurt high-speed rail line</a>. At the same time local and regional rail services were based at the existing underground station, now renamed <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_regional_station" title="Frankfurt Airport regional station">Frankfurt Airport regional station</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Closure_of_the_Rhein-Main_Air_Base">Closure of the Rhein-Main Air Base</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Closure of the Rhein-Main Air Base">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 30 December 2005, the Rhein-Main Air Base in the southern part of the airport ground was closed and the US Air Force moved to <a href="/wiki/Ramstein_Air_Base" title="Ramstein Air Base">Ramstein Air Base</a>. The property was handed back to Fraport which allows the airport to use it to build a new passenger terminal. The property of the housing area for the soldiers, called <i>Gateway Gardens</i>, which was located north-east of the airport site, was given back to the city of Frankfurt in the same year and will be developed as a business district in the following years.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Airbus_A380_and_The_Squaire">The Airbus A380 and <i>The Squaire</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: The Airbus A380 and The Squaire">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>From 2005 to 2007, a large <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> maintenance facility was built at Frankfurt Airport because Lufthansa wanted to station their future A380 aircraft fleet there. Both terminals also underwent major renovations in order to handle the A380, including the installation of a third boarding bridge at several gates. Lufthansa\'s first Airbus A380 went into operation in June 2010 and was named <i>Frankfurt am Main</i>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_View_of_Frankfurt_Airport_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Aerial_View_of_Frankfurt_Airport_1.jpg/220px-Aerial_View_of_Frankfurt_Airport_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Aerial_View_of_Frankfurt_Airport_1.jpg/330px-Aerial_View_of_Frankfurt_Airport_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Aerial_View_of_Frankfurt_Airport_1.jpg/440px-Aerial_View_of_Frankfurt_Airport_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2289" data-file-height="1100" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aerial_View_of_Frankfurt_Airport_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of the central airport buildings including <i>The Squaire</i> in the back</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2011, a large office building called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Squaire" title="The Squaire">The Squaire</a></i> (a blend of <i>square</i> and <i>air</i>) opened at Frankfurt Airport. It was built on top of the Airport long-distance station and is considered the largest office building in Germany with 140,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (1,500,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) floor area. Main tenants are <a href="/wiki/KPMG" title="KPMG">KPMG</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Hilton_Hotels_%26_Resorts" title="Hilton Hotels &amp; Resorts">Hilton Hotels</a>.\n</p><p>Since 2012, the <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">people mover</a> "The Squaire Metro" connects the Squaire with the nine-storey parking structure. On a length of about 300 metres the so-called <a href="/wiki/MiniMetro" title="MiniMetro">MiniMetro</a> system with its two cabins can carry up to 1,300 passengers per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The constructor of the system was the Italian <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturer</a> <a href="/wiki/Leitner_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Leitner Group">Leitner</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_fourth_runway">The fourth runway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The fourth runway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Plans to build a fourth runway at Frankfurt Airport were underway in 1997, but owing to violent conflicts with the concept Fraport let residents\' groups and environmentalists participate in the process to find a mutually acceptable solution. In 2000, a task force presented their conclusion which generally approved a new runway, but of shorter length (only 2.8 kilometres compared to the other three 4-kilometre-long runways), which would serve as a landing-only runway for smaller aircraft. Additional requirements included improved noise protection arrangements and a strict ban on night flights between 11&#160;pm and 5&#160;am across the whole airport. In 2001, Fraport applied for approval to build the new runway, with three possible options. The conclusion was that a runway north-west of the airport site would have the least impact on local residents and the surrounding environment. The plans were approved by the Hessian government in December 2007, but the requested ban on night flights was lifted because it was argued that an international airport like Frankfurt would need night flights, especially for worldwide <a href="/wiki/Freight" class="mw-redirect" title="Freight">freight</a> transport. Construction of the new 2,800&#160;m (9,186&#160;ft) long <i>Runway Northwest</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Kelsterbach" title="Kelsterbach">Kelsterbach</a> Forest began in early 2009.\n</p><p>In 2012, the website <i>Airport Watch</i> reports weekly protests have been occurring at the airport since the opening of a fourth runway a year previously.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Developments_since_2011">Developments since 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Developments since 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The new runway officially went into operation on 20 October 2011, with an aircraft carrying <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">Chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>, performing the first landing on 21 October. The centre line separation from the existing north runway is about 1,400&#160;m (4,593&#160;ft). This allows simultaneous instrument landing system (ILS) operations on these two runways, which has not been possible on the other parallel runways, which do not meet the 3,500 feet (1,100&#160;m) minimum separation for ILS operations.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> This allowed the airport to increase its capacity from 83 to 126 aircraft movements per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 October 2011, the Hessian Administration Court ruled that night flights between 11pm and 5am (the so-called <i>Mediationsnacht</i>) are no longer allowed at Frankfurt Airport after the inauguration of the new runway, and therefore overrode the approval from the Hessian government from 2007 which allowed 17 scheduled flights per night. On 4 April 2012, the German Administrative Court confirmed the decision of the Hessian Administration Court, banning night flights between 11pm and 5am.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To handle the predicted passenger amount of about 90&#160;million in 2020, a new terminal section adjacent to Terminal 1 for an additional six million passengers opened on 10 October 2012. It is called <i>Flugsteig A-Plus</i> and exclusively used by Lufthansa mainly for their long-haul flights. Flugsteig A-Plus features eight parking positions that are able to handle four Airbus A380s or seven <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-8" title="Boeing 747-8">Boeing 747-8</a>/<a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">747-400</a> at once.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2016, <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> announced the opening of a new base at Frankfurt Airport with four routes to <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>. This move by Ryanair was heavily blasted, especially by Lufthansa, as Ryanair was granted high discounts and incentives regarding the airport\'s fees.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On 28 February 2017, Ryanair announced its winter programme for Frankfurt which will see a further 20 new routes being added.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="COVID-19_pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: COVID-19 pandemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Portions of the airport were closed in early 2020 due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>. The Northwest Runway and Runway 18 West were closed on March 23 and re-purposed for parking unused aircraft. Terminal 2 was also closed, and all passenger operations were concentrated in Terminal 1. The Northwest Runway re-opened in July to handle summer tourist demand, while Runway 18 West remained closed.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> With almost no passenger traffic in the spring months, Frankfurt\'s total passenger volume in 2020 fell to 18.8 million, the lowest figure recorded since 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Frankfurt Airport has two large main passenger terminals (1 and 2) and a much smaller dedicated First Class Terminal which is operated and exclusively used by Lufthansa. As is the case at <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London\xe2\x80\x93Heathrow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Tokyo\xe2\x80\x93Narita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Pearson_International_Airport" title="Toronto Pearson International Airport">Toronto\xe2\x80\x93Pearson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles</a> (bar the Tom Bradley International Terminal) and <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">Chicago\xe2\x80\x93O\'Hare</a>\'s future Global Terminal, terminal operations are grouped for airlines and <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">airline alliances</a> rather than into domestic and international routes.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Flughafen,_Terminal_1,_landside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Terminal_1%2C_landside.jpg/220px-Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Terminal_1%2C_landside.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Terminal_1%2C_landside.jpg/330px-Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Terminal_1%2C_landside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Terminal_1%2C_landside.jpg/440px-Frankfurt_Flughafen%2C_Terminal_1%2C_landside.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1288" data-file-height="966" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Flughafen,_Terminal_1,_landside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 1</div></div></div>\n<p>Terminal 1 is the older and larger one of the two passenger terminals. The <a href="/wiki/Landside" class="mw-redirect" title="Landside">landside</a> is 420 metres long. It has been enlarged several times and is divided into concourses <i>A</i>, <i>B</i>, <i>C</i> and <i>Z</i> and has a capacity of approximately 50&#160;million passengers per year. Terminal 1 is functionally divided into three levels, the departures level on the upper floor with check-in counters, the arrivals level with baggage claim areas on the ground floor and, underneath, a distribution floor with access to the <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport_regional_station" title="Frankfurt Airport regional station">regional station</a> and underground and multilevel parking. Departures and arrivals levels each have separate street approaches. A bus station is located at arrivals level. Terminal 1 has a total of 103 gates, which include 54 gates equipped with jetways (25 in Concourse A, 18 in Concourse B, 11 in Concourse C). Concourse <i>Z</i> sits on top of Concourse <i>A</i> sharing the same jet bridges between both concourses. Flights to non-Schengen destinations depart from the <i>Z</i> gates and Schengen flights depart from the <i>A</i> gates.\n</p><p>Pier A was extended by 500 metres in 2000, and a link between Terminal 1 and Terminal 2, as well as the Hall C extension opened in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 10 October 2012, an 800-metre-long westward expansion of Terminal 1 called <i>Pier A-Plus</i> went into operation. It provides more stands for <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">wide-body aircraft</a> like the Airbus A380.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Terminal 1 is primarily used by Lufthansa, its associated companies (<a href="/wiki/Brussels_Airlines" title="Brussels Airlines">Brussels Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_Air_Lines" title="Swiss International Air Lines">Swiss International Air Lines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Airlines" title="Austrian Airlines">Austrian Airlines</a>) and its <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> partners (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada" title="Air Canada">Air Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_China" title="Air China">Air China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_India" title="Air India">Air India</a>, <a href="/wiki/All_Nippon_Airways" title="All Nippon Airways">All Nippon Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asiana_Airlines" title="Asiana Airlines">Asiana Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatia_Airlines" title="Croatia Airlines">Croatia Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egyptair" title="Egyptair">Egyptair</a>, <a href="/wiki/LOT_Polish_Airlines" title="LOT Polish Airlines">LOT Polish Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_African_Airways" title="South African Airways">South African Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/TAP_Air_Portugal" title="TAP Air Portugal">TAP Air Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways" title="Thai Airways">Thai Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a>).\n</p><p>Some airlines that are not part of the <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Group" title="Lufthansa Group">Lufthansa Group</a> or Star Alliance also use Terminal 1. They include <a href="/wiki/Air_Malta" title="Air Malta">Air Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_Air" title="Bulgaria Air">Bulgaria Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran_Air" title="Iran Air">Iran Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oman_Air" title="Oman Air">Oman Air</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunisair" title="Tunisair">Tunisair</a> among others.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> member airlines <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Airlines" title="Middle East Airlines">Middle East Airlines</a> also use Terminal 1 (Concourses B and C).\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Flughafen_Terminal_2.20130901.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Frankfurt_Flughafen_Terminal_2.20130901.jpg/220px-Frankfurt_Flughafen_Terminal_2.20130901.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Frankfurt_Flughafen_Terminal_2.20130901.jpg/330px-Frankfurt_Flughafen_Terminal_2.20130901.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Frankfurt_Flughafen_Terminal_2.20130901.jpg/440px-Frankfurt_Flughafen_Terminal_2.20130901.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3999" data-file-height="2151" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt_Flughafen_Terminal_2.20130901.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 2</div></div></div>\n<p>Terminal 2, which has a capacity of 15&#160;million passengers a year, was opened in 1994 and is divided into concourses <i>D</i> and <i>E</i>. A continuous concourse between Terminal 1C and 2D provides direct, but non-public access between the two terminals. It has eight gates with jetways and 34 apron stands, a total of 42 gates and is able to handle wide-body aircraft such as the Airbus A380.\n</p><p>Terminal 2 is primarily used by airlines of the <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">oneworld</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnair" title="Finnair">Finnair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iberia" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia">Iberia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines" title="Malaysia Airlines">Malaysia Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Maroc" title="Royal Air Maroc">Royal Air Maroc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Jordanian" title="Royal Jordanian">Royal Jordanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/S7_Airlines" title="S7 Airlines">S7 Airlines</a>) and <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> alliances (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Airlines" title="China Airlines">China Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Eastern_Airlines" title="China Eastern Airlines">China Eastern Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Airlines" title="Czech Airlines">Czech Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garuda_Indonesia" title="Garuda Indonesia">Garuda Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_Air" title="Korean Air">Korean Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudia" title="Saudia">Saudia</a>, <a href="/wiki/TAROM" title="TAROM">TAROM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_Airlines" title="Vietnam Airlines">Vietnam Airlines</a>; note that SkyTeam members <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Airlines" title="Middle East Airlines">Middle East Airlines</a> operate out of Terminal 1, in concourses B and C).\n</p><p>Terminal 2 is also used by airlines that do not belong to any of the three major airline alliances, including <a href="/wiki/Air_Moldova" title="Air Moldova">Air Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Serbia" title="Air Serbia">Air Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/China_Southern_Airlines" title="China Southern Airlines">China Southern Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Airways" title="Kuwait Airways">Kuwait Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/LATAM_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="LATAM Airlines">LATAM Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Somon_Air" title="Somon Air">Somon Air</a>, among others.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_overview">Terminal overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Terminal overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable zebra">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Terminal</th>\n<th>Concourse</th>\n<th>Schengen gates</th>\n<th>Non-Schengen gates</th>\n<th>Location\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="4">1\n</td>\n<td>1A\n</td>\n<td>A1-A69\n</td>\n<td>\n</td>\n<td>Terminal 1, western concourse, lower departure concourse\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SkyLine">SkyLine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: SkyLine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Passengers and visitors can change terminals with the people mover system <a href="/wiki/SkyLine_(Frankfurt)" title="SkyLine (Frankfurt)">SkyLine</a> which has the following stops:\n</p>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable zebra">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Stop</th>\n<th>Restrictions\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1AZ</td>\n<td>passengers only\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1B</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1C</td>\n<td>non-Schengen passengers only\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2DE</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<p>The travel time between the terminals is 2 minutes with trains arriving every 2\xe2\x80\x933 minutes during the day. Additionally there is regular bus service between the terminals.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways">Runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Frankfurt Airport has four runways of which three are arranged parallel in east\xe2\x80\x93west direction and one in north\xe2\x80\x93south direction. In 2010 three runways (Runways North, South and West) handled 464,432 aircraft movements, which equated to 83 movements per hour. With the start of operation of the Northwest Runway in October 2011 the airport was predicted to be able to handle 126 movements per hour. It is predicted that aircraft movements will increase up to 700,000 in the year 2020. By using the fourth runway, Frankfurt Airport is able for the first time to handle simultaneous parallel landings, because the distance between the north and the north-west runways is 1,400&#160;m (4,593&#160;ft). Simultaneous parallel landings were not possible with the north and south runway pairing, because the separation distance did not meet the safety standards.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable zebra">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Direction <br />(Name)</th>\n<th>Length&#160;\xc3\x97&#160;Width<br />in m (ft)</th>\n<th>Surface</th>\n<th>Orientation</th>\n<th>Start of operation</th>\n<th>Use\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>07C/25C</b> <br />(Runway&#160;North)\n</td>\n<td>4000 \xc3\x97 60 <br />(13,123 \xc3\x97 197)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Asphalt_concrete" title="Asphalt concrete">Asphalt</a>\n</td>\n<td>East-west\n</td>\n<td>1936\n</td>\n<td>Take-offs (landings allowed)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>07R/25L</b> <br />(Runway&#160;South)\n</td>\n<td>4000 \xc3\x97 45 <br />(13,123 \xc3\x97 148)\n</td>\n<td>Asphalt\n</td>\n<td>East-west\n</td>\n<td>1949\n</td>\n<td>Take-offs and landings\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>18</b> <br />(Runway&#160;West)\n</td>\n<td>4000 \xc3\x97 45 <br />(13,123 \xc3\x97 148)\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Concrete" title="Concrete">Concrete</a>\n</td>\n<td>North-south\n</td>\n<td>1984\n</td>\n<td>Take-offs in southbound direction only\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><b>07L/25R</b> <br />(Runway&#160;Northwest)\n</td>\n<td>2800 \xc3\x97 45 <br />(9,240 \xc3\x97 148)\n</td>\n<td>Concrete\n</td>\n<td>East-west\n</td>\n<td>2011\n</td>\n<td>Landings only (not allowed for <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a>, <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-11" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-11">MD-11</a>)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<p>During normal operation the two outer parallel runways (07L/25R and 07R/25L) are used for landings and the central parallel runway (07C/25C) and the Runway West (18) for take-offs. The three parallel runways have two markings because they can be operated in two directions while the Runway West can only be used in one direction.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_expansions">Future expansions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Future expansions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt-Main_Airport_Map_EN.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Frankfurt-Main_Airport_Map_EN.png/220px-Frankfurt-Main_Airport_Map_EN.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Frankfurt-Main_Airport_Map_EN.png/330px-Frankfurt-Main_Airport_Map_EN.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Frankfurt-Main_Airport_Map_EN.png/440px-Frankfurt-Main_Airport_Map_EN.png 2x" data-file-width="2253" data-file-height="1890" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Frankfurt-Main_Airport_Map_EN.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Airport map with planned and already constructed expansions</div></div></div>\n<h4><span id="Terminal_3_.28under_construction.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_3_(under_construction)">Terminal 3 (under construction)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Terminal 3 (under construction)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2009, the German government decided to create third terminals for both Frankfurt Airport and <a href="/wiki/Munich_Airport" title="Munich Airport">Munich Airport</a> in order to handle expected passenger flows of 90&#160;million in Frankfurt by 2020 and 50&#160;million in Munich by 2017. The new terminal is scheduled to be built by Fraport, south of the existing terminals on the grounds of the former Rhein-Main Air Base. The new <i>Terminal 3</i> is to accommodate up to 25&#160;million passengers and will feature 75 new aircraft positions when completely constructed. An extension of the <i>SkyLine</i> people mover system is planned to connect the new terminal to Terminals 1 and 2 and the airport train stations.\n</p><p>In August 2014, the city of Frankfurt granted building permission for the first phase of Terminal 3.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The groundbreaking for the new terminal took place on 5 October 2015. Its first phase, consisting of the main building and two of the planned four piers (concourses 3H and 3J), is planned to open by 2026 and will be able to handle 15&#160;million additional passengers per year. Total costs are estimated at 3&#160;billion euros.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, Frankfurt Airport first indicated that the second-phase construction of the easternmost pier (concourse 3G) could be moved forward so that low-cost carriers can use this pier from 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> After approval by municipal authorities in 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> the piers will be constructed and used according to the following timetable:<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\nDue to the COVID-19 pandemic, Fraport postponed the opening of the new terminal to 2026 in March 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Concourse 3G</b> (easternmost pier):\n</p>\n<ul><li>Construction of first twelve bus gates, reachable via shuttle buses from terminals 1/2, in use by 2021</li>\n<li>Construction of additional twelve bus gates by 2023/2024</li>\n<li>Construction of passenger <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jet bridges</a> by 2025/2026</li></ul>\n<p><b>Check-in area, concourses 3H and 3J</b> (central piers): Construction by 2023 including transport systems for visitors, passengers and luggage to the other terminals\n</p>\n<ul><li>Concourse 3H is planned for Schengen flights</li>\n<li>Concourse 3J is planned for non-Schengen flights<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p><b>Concourse 3K</b> (westernmost pier): Possible third-phase expansion depending on development of passenger numbers\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_Transport_System">Passenger Transport System</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Passenger Transport System">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>A new passenger transport system is planned for the connection of the new terminal 3 and the existing terminals 1 and 2. It will use a track which is separate from the existing SkyLine people mover but will allow for interchanges between them.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> It is scheduled to have four stops in the final stage:\n</p>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable zebra">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Stop</th>\n<th>Location/remarks\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>F</td>\n<td>Long- and short-distance railway station\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1C</td>\n<td>Interchange station to SkyLine (long-term planning)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2DE</td>\n<td>Interchange station to SkyLine (upon inauguration of PTS)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>3GHJK</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Frankfurt_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Lufthansa and their <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> partners account for the majority of all traffic at Frankfurt Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-2011Statistics_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011Statistics-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The following airlines offer year-round and seasonal scheduled
